Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 135

— (Xie Zhongwen)

Ordinary people are despised, while special people are admired. This is because there are too many ordinary people and ordinary things in the world, and too few special people and special things.

When ordinary people remain poor, it is ordinary; when officials become rich, it is special. Wearing cloth clothes and eating coarse rice is ordinary; wearing silk and satin and eating delicacies is special.

However, without the ordinary, the special would not stand out. The special originates from the ordinary. Without ordinary people, where would officials come from? Without people wearing cloth clothes and eating coarse rice to work, where would silk and satin and delicacies come from? It can be seen that the ordinary should not be despised, and the value of the special should sometimes be lowered.

It is precisely because there are so many ordinary people that they constitute the true members of society. It is precisely because there are so many ordinary things that they are the main part of social life. The ordinary should originally be valued!

The ordinary is the master, the special is the vassal.

Disaster Relief 136

— Luo Zheng

It is truly unfortunate to be Chinese. One year of man-made disasters, one year of natural disasters. Floods have just passed, and drought follows. The severe drought has just been avoided, but the great flood has arrived again. This year, in the early summer, none of us expected that there would be another drought, but who knew that after not many days of continuous rain, it showed signs of a great flood. Mountain floods broke out, dikes collapsed, and many places became swamps. People and livestock were adrift, and houses were destroyed. Tens of millions of disaster victims were homeless. The cries for help are unbearable to hear.

Now, several enthusiastic philanthropists have recently gone to Beijing to participate in disaster relief meetings to discuss solutions. At the same time, the government has also allocated huge sums of money from the Ministry of Finance for distribution and relief. Although these are far from enough for the tens of millions of disaster victims, they can at least temporarily avoid starvation. For those disaster victims, it is no less than drinking a drop of nectar.

But Shanghai is paradise, and the people who live in Shanghai are always so happy. Floods have nothing to do with them, and drought has nothing to do with them. In short, no natural or man-made disasters will befall them, so they will never think of the suffering of the people in hell. But I always hope that they will unfold these pictures of misery and take a look. If everyone still has a conscience, then they should also save some of their enjoyment money to help the countless homeless, unclothed, and hungry refugees, so as not to let them become wailing wild geese and starving corpses by the roadside!

However, I also have some humble opinions on disaster relief methods that I would like to contribute to the authorities responsible for disaster relief: that is, first of all, the shortcomings of past imperfect management should be eliminated. On the one hand, it is necessary to inspect the situation in the disaster area and distribute relief, and on the other hand, it is necessary to strictly prevent anyone from engaging in corruption. How much is raised should be distributed, and there should be no waste of a single penny except for necessary expenses. This is the only way to make people with money willing to enthusiastically contribute, and those disaster victims will also receive practical benefits.

Water 137

— Zhu Ying

Water, in this world, is everywhere except in the endless deserts. It seems to be the most unremarkable thing, so most people seem to think of water as a very ordinary thing. But water is really the thing that has the greatest relationship to our lives.

Readers, do you still remember? Last summer, in several provinces in the southeast, not a drop of rain fell. The farmland cracked, and in some places the seedlings withered from the drought, and there was no harvest. During that period, in the countryside of the drought area, the farmers took the last spoonful of water from every pond and lake, treaded it with waterwheels or sucked it with spray pumps, and irrigated it into the farmland, trying to maintain the life of the seedlings on which the lives of the whole family depended. Even the flowing water was gradually sucked away by the farmers day by day, and the water level gradually dropped until light boats would kiss the bottom of the river. Just think, at that time, how valuable was "water"? "Water" was, for the farmers, not just indirectly for the farmers, almost an invaluable treasure beyond life.

However, "water" is not necessarily valuable to humans. Sometimes it is considered a great harm to humans. Not to mention past historical events, just look at the recent great wind and rain that hit Kyushu, Japan, and the flooding of our Yangtze River basin, and the other face of "water" should be deeply recognized by the general public.

That's right, "water" is an invaluable treasure beyond human life, but sometimes it is cursed by people. What's the reason for this? Well, "water" is indeed a very ordinary thing, but in reality, it also cannot escape the economic law of "demand" and "supply."

Smoke Emission and Coal Adding 138

— Juan Yin

Hungry Ghost 139

— Feng Moni

"Ah! A hungry ghost."

"How scary, like a skeleton with skin stretched over it."

"Hey! How pitiful."

A group of people were talking. A man was lying on a reed mat on the sidewalk, almost lifeless. His hands and feet were like thin bamboo poles, and his skin had turned gray-white. His eye sockets were sunken, his eyelids were closed, and white foam was flowing from the corner of his mouth. His withered hands were still twitching. Everyone who saw this person felt sorry for him, because he had nothing to eat and was about to starve to death.

"Please do a good deed! He's starving to death!" A woman sitting on the reed mat was pleading with the many people in the crowd.

There were many people in the crowd, but they only expressed sympathy and were unwilling to help, just watching a person who was about to starve to death.

Over there was the Qingpingyuan Restaurant, packed with diners. The kitchen was exceptionally busy, and the pots were constantly clanging. Steaming hot dishes were sent to each diner. Even while eating, they still felt bored. A prostitute with a snake-like body came over, and after eating, she giggled and laughed, supporting the prostitute as she got into a car. They didn't know that on the sidewalk across the street, a person was lying on a reed mat, about to die.

The withered human form gradually stopped twitching and finally died. He was a hungry ghost.

"Hey! He's dead! Please do a good deed!" A woman sitting on the reed mat looked at the man's corpse beside her and pleaded with the many people in the crowd.

"Ah! Truly a hungry ghost."

"How scary, look: like a skeleton with skin stretched over it."

"Ah! Ultimately pitiful."

There were many people in the crowd, but they only expressed sympathy and were unwilling to help, and they watched this person breathe his last breath.

Over there, the Qingpingyuan Restaurant was still so lively, packed with diners, but they didn't know that there was such a hungry ghost on the sidewalk across the street who had died from lack of food!

Royal Incense Record 140

— Originally written by Princess De Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

One night, it was originally my turn to be on duty. Although Elder Lady's worries had been removed, so I no longer had to worry. But on one hand, sitting on the floor made it fundamentally difficult to fall asleep; on the other hand, my heart was occupied with tomorrow's trip to the lake, making it even harder to close my eyes. So I forced myself to vaguely hold out until early the third morning. Early morning here refers to an unambiguous time, around three or four o'clock. The Empress Dowager and everyone else all got up. By the time everyone was neatly packed and swarming onto the Empress Dowager's imperial boat, slowly floating on Kunming Lake, there was still a while before the sun rose! Today, the Empress Dowager's throne was comparatively high and placed in the center of the bow. Behind it, there were many small low stools arranged for us ladies-in-waiting to sit. Our boat was still being punted with bamboo poles, slowly drifting towards the north of Kunming Lake without leaning to either side. The lotus flowers were grown most densely there, and the lotus leaves looked like a green carpet spread on the water. Then, the Empress Dowager said very gently:

"Stop the boat! Everyone be quiet, watch, and listen!"

The scene at this time could be said to have a very mysterious meaning. In the east, although part of the sky was pleasantly dyed with a long streak of color, the sun's head was still hiding below, not yet peeking out. The gray-brown night was gradually moving westward, handing over the position it occupied bit by bit. A few wisps of black smoke curled in mid-air, like the sash of the god of night. Many kingfishers were flying on both sides of us, but not singing, seemingly quietly enjoying the celestial music of the early morning. (385)

Chapter 17 Do Not Ask a Daughter's Body to Hide Unspeakable Pain Compete to See a Noble Person's Face to Admire the High Style Together

Local Customs and Scenery

Memoirs of an Open-Air Cinema 142

— Shanghai Dispatch

It's that time of year again. The Racecourse Cinema, the Garden Cinema, and the Cangzhou Hotel Garden Cinema are appearing one after another, embellishing this metropolis for the summer season. Here, we analyze one thing: these three open-air cinemas can be divided into two categories. The first category is the Garden Cinema, which is open as usual this year because it has appeared in previous summers. The second category is the other two; presumably, tourists who like to go to new places have a special impression of them from 1935.

This brings up a small question: what was the distribution of open-air cinemas like in earlier years? If we bring it up, perhaps it will suddenly remind today's night owls of the old days? So, the Shanghai Dispatch opened the parchment book and wrote its answer with a quill pen—

1924 was the year that Shanghai began to have open-air cinemas. "Summer Cinema," on Bazhi Road, was the pioneer of this novelty. In the same year, the St. George Open-Air Cinema closed, in the garden of the St. George Hotel at the end of Jing'an Temple Road. At that time, the starting point of the only public bus route in the Public Concession, operated by Mr. Dong Hansheng, was at the entrance of St. George. Those who pay attention to traffic conditions can still recall it. The backstage boss of the St. George Open-Air Cinema was the then-famous Aipu Factory Cinema, which had strong strength and carefully selected films. The Summer Cinema could not withstand its pressure and disappeared in the second year. However, now that the St. George Hotel has changed hands and the Aipu Factory has long been outdated and eliminated, past events only make people recall it in vain.

The market is always competitive. In the summer of 1925, St. George reappeared with the triumphant posture of defeating the Summer Cinema, and the Dahua Open-Air Cinema also brought the backstage boss of the Shanghai Grand Theatre to become its strong rival. This new open-air silver palace was located in the Italian Garden inside the Dahua Hotel on Gordon Road; the environment was almost exactly the same as the St. George Garden. The place where the Dahua Hotel was located was originally McBain Garden, which was famous in Shanghai for its magnificence. It was bought by someone in 1924 and turned into a hotel, named Dahua. In the autumn of 1931, the Dahua Hotel was sold and demolished, waiting for a price to be negotiated, but no one has asked about it until now. The land has been opened up by the Municipal Council in time to create Dahua and McBain Roads, forming a cross shape, which has become famous. From the opening to the demolition of the Dahua Hotel, the Dahua Open-Air Cinema opened on time every summer for the audience.

The Garden Cinema opened on a large lawn of the Zhafei Road Ball Club, which is the only open-air cinema in the French Concession, and it is also open this year to welcome people in. It started in 1932, but the open-air silver palace on the Ball Club lawn did not originate in 1932: in the summer of 1926, this lawn was used by the Verdun Open-Air Cinema. Tracing the roots, this place of the Ball Club was originally the German Garden, which was confiscated by the French during the European War and turned into a park, named Verdun. It was not until 1926 that it became the new site of the French Ball Club. Some people call it the French Business New Ball Club, and that's why. The cinema in 1926 was called Verdun, and that's why.

Understanding the difficulties and prosperity of the past, knowing the value of the present; the Shanghai Dispatch has thus closed its parchment book.

Ministry of Education Explains the Doubts about the Examination of Secondary School and Normal School Teachers 143

Two documents from the Ministry of Education replying to the Shandong Provincial Department of Education and explaining the doubts about the examination of secondary school and normal school teachers are compiled as follows: (A) Regarding the various doubts about the examination of secondary school and normal school teachers, they are hereby reviewed and instructed as follows: (1) The so-called proficient skills must be proven to be true. If the performance is presented and the results are feared to be untrue, the examiner may be ordered to submit other documents that can be used as proof. As for the usual teaching performance, it should be based on the records reported by the inspector to the department. (2) Self-edited or translated lecture notes and supplementary teaching materials within the scope of the subject taught, if they are indeed excellent, can be regarded as research achievements. (3) Graduates before the registration is established, whose graduation qualifications have not been reported to the Ministry for retroactive recognition, cannot be considered valid. (B) Secondary school and normal school teachers who have no examiners, the subject voluntarily undertaken should be based on the subject they specialize in, but if the subject they also study is indeed excellent, they may also be allowed to be examined without examiners.

Measures for the Exhibition of Achievements in Children's Health 144

The measures for the exhibition of achievements in children's health passed by the previous general meeting of the National Children's Year Implementation Committee are as follows:

1. The purpose of this meeting is to enable children and their parents and the public to understand the health status of the children themselves, to find ways to promote or correct them, and to arouse children's interest, attention, and efforts in healthy living.

2. The date and location of the exhibition shall be negotiated and handled by the local Children's Year responsible agency in cooperation with the local school in a suitable location at any time.

3. The materials for the exhibition are divided into the following items: A. Children's own labor achievements, (1) health achievements, (2) health books, (3) health activity photos, (4) health models and specimens, (5) health toys, (6) other health symbols and equipment. B. Achievements in conducting children's health education and activities, (1) equipment in the school health room, (2) statistical charts of children's diseases and physical defects, (3) reference health books, (4) reference health models and specimens, (5) borrowed or purchased children's toys, (6) others (such as photos of health education work, etc.) During the exhibition, parent-child gatherings, recreational parties, and other gatherings may be held, with the principle of being able to convene the parents of children to attend the meeting. 5. Before the meeting, the responsible agency shall invite experts or local celebrities to attend the meeting on a regular basis for evaluation, and a review book shall also be prepared in the venue for public evaluation by the audience as a reference for the invited reviewers. 6. The agency responsible for hosting the exhibition shall make its own awards or solicit awards to reward the most outstanding performers. 7. When necessary, the exhibits may be exhibited on tour in order to arouse widespread attention from the society. 8. Various publicity work should be carried out before and after the content of the exhibition and the course of the meeting in order to arouse social attention. 9. The expenses required for the exhibition shall be raised by the local Children's Year responsible agency.

Implementation Plan for Compulsory Education (Part 1) (Lei Zhen's Speech on the Central Radio Station) 148

What I am reporting today is the compulsory education that is being implemented. The meaning of compulsory education is that the state uses laws to stipulate that all school-age children (referring to children from six to twelve years old) in the country must receive the minimum education. From the state's point of view, running compulsory education is an obligation that should be fulfilled to the people. The people enjoy this kind of education as a right. The state provides this kind of education to improve healthy people and improve the qualifications of citizens, so it contains the meaning of compulsion. Most civilized countries in Europe and the United States have laws to punish people who do not comply.

My country's people are ignorant and urgently need to implement compulsory education, which has long been noticed by the general public. However, due to the lack of political track and the extreme economic difficulties, those who care about education cannot start. Sun Yat-sen also said, "...All young men and women in autonomous regions have the right to education. The tuition fees, books, and the clothing and food of the students should be provided by the public." He also said, "...Socialist scholars advocate equality of education. All people in the society, regardless of their poverty, can enter public schools. Not only do they not charge tuition fees, but the expenses of clothing, shoes, and books are also borne by the public, so that the people can use their intelligence and talents to learn all subjects..." It can be seen that the need for compulsory education in our country has long been noticed by those who are aware of it. However, in today's domestic social situation, the people are poor and the resources are exhausted. The right to education is only exclusively occupied by a small number of people. The vast majority of impoverished children have their right to education deprived by economic oppression. Therefore, the vast majority of the people are illiterate and have no knowledge. They live in a romantic, decadent, lazy, and dirty life. Not only do they not know how to pull themselves out, but they regard it as natural. How can we talk to such people about exercising civil rights? How can we talk about jointly shouldering the responsibility of saving the country and the nation?

Today, China is facing a series of disasters caused by both natural disasters and human activities. Foreign neighbors are pressing closer day by day, and the national situation is in extreme danger. At this extraordinary time, saving the country and seeking survival is the responsibility of the entire nation, and it is also a matter of life and death for our entire nation. In order to meet our own needs for survival and to cope with the adverse international environment, we can only awaken ourselves and find our own way to survival and move forward. The important condition for survival is to cultivate healthy citizens, so that the entire nation has the general knowledge suitable for survival and increase their necessary living abilities. To achieve this goal, we should all work hard to carry out the road to eliminate illiteracy, and use the power of education to cultivate the Chinese nation, which is struggling in suffering and eking out a living, so that it can change from unconscious to conscious, from the old and sick man, the nation despised by the world, to a brand-new Chinese nation. This is our due effort and also a wonderful medicine for resurrection.

This time, the government has made the greatest determination to plan and promote compulsory education with all its strength. It is the government's due obligation, but the people's wisdom has not been developed and the funds are limited. We must also work together with the people of the whole country, and each person should do his best to help, so that it can proceed smoothly "step by step according to the regulations" and achieve the final goal.

Assuming that the total population of China is 400 million, with one school-age child in every ten people, there should be 40 million school-age children in the country. According to the statistics of elementary education in the 20th year, the number of elementary school children in the country is more than 11.6 million, and the number of school-age children who are out of school is about 30 million. The number of children in school only accounts for 23% of the school-age children. It can be seen the importance of implementing compulsory education, especially in this time of internal and external troubles. The general public cannot receive the minimum national education, so no matter what is said about political construction or material construction, it is all in vain.

Our Kuomintang deeply understands this point, so at the fifth plenary session of the fourth Central Executive Committee, it was resolved to implement compulsory education and treat both the symptoms and the root causes. The Ministry of Education has followed the promulgation of the General Outline of Measures for the First Phase of Compulsory Education and the General Outline of Measures for the Short-Term Compulsory Education, ordering the education authorities of all provinces and cities to comply with the implementation. This year, it has formulated the Provisional General Outline of Measures for the Implementation of Compulsory Education and the General Outline of Measures for the Distribution of Central Compulsory Education Funds in the 24th year of the Republic of China, and issued them to the education authorities of all provinces and cities for compliance and ordered them to prepare detailed plans to report to the Ministry for reference. Now I will report a summary of the provisional measures for the implementation of compulsory education and funding, and I hope that all compatriots in the country will help to carry out the project.

I. The Purpose of Compulsory Education

Compulsory education should follow the educational purpose of the Republic of China and its implementation guidelines, meet the needs of the actual life of the people, pay attention to the development of national consciousness and national concepts, so that all school-age children in the country (referring to children aged six to twelve) gradually receive one-year, two-year, or four-year compulsory education within a ten-year period.

II. Measures for Compulsory Enrollment and Postponement and Exemption from School

In places where ordinary elementary schools and short-term elementary schools are enough to accommodate local school-age children, all healthy school-age children must enter ordinary elementary schools or short-term elementary schools.

As for school-age children who have diseases or other reasons that temporarily prevent them from attending school, their parents or guardians may request a postponement of school with a certificate. If they have chronic diseases that make them unable to receive education, their parents or guardians may request an exemption from school with a certificate.

For children who should enroll but do not enroll, their parents or guardians should be given a written warning for a certain period of time, requiring them to enroll. Otherwise, their names will be posted for public display. If they still do not comply, the county or city education administrative agency may request the county government to impose a fine of one to five yuan and still require them to enroll within a time limit. The aforementioned fines will still be used for the purpose of compulsory education.

III. Procedures for Implementing Compulsory Education

In the 24th year of the Republic of China, all provinces and cities should order their subordinate counties and cities to delineate elementary school districts according to the original population of rural villages and towns, and run short-term elementary schools. Each elementary school district should have an average population of about 1,000 people. Within every five to ten elementary school districts, an ordinary elementary school should be gradually established. The same applies to municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan.

According to the reports of various provinces and cities, it is estimated that more than 60,000 short-term elementary schools should be run this year. However, due to the difficulty in raising funds, the actual number that can be established will definitely be slightly less than the planned number. However, according to recent statistics, there should be at least 40,000 schools. Assuming that each school can accommodate 100 students, it can rescue 4 million children who are out of school.

The implementation of compulsory education is divided into three phases.

Phase 1: From August of the 24th year of the Republic of China to July of the 29th year, all older children who are out of school and school-age children who have not enrolled should receive at least one year of compulsory education. In order to provide children with one year of compulsory education, all provinces and cities should carry out the following matters:

(1) Promote short-term elementary schools: order all elementary school districts to set up one-year short-term elementary schools at the planned school locations, and recruit out-of-school children aged nine to twelve. This type of elementary school is based on the principle of adopting a two-part system, with half-day or full-day teaching in the morning and afternoon each day, with at least three hours or four hours of teaching. The duration of study is one year. Rural short-term elementary schools may have agricultural holidays. Ordinary elementary schools and other schools and public agencies may also set up short-term elementary school classes.

(2) Improve private schools: order all places to organize and improve the original private schools, and uniformly follow the curriculum of short-term elementary schools or ordinary elementary schools, and rename them improved private schools. The better ones may be changed to short-term elementary schools or ordinary elementary schools.

Pilot mobile education: order local authorities to set up mobile teachers to teach out-of-school children in poor and remote areas with inconvenient transportation, with the same level as short-term elementary schools. By the end of this phase, at least 80% of the total number of school-age children should have received one year of short-term elementary school education or equivalent education.

Phase 2: From August of the 29th year of the Republic of China to July of the 33rd year, all school-age children should receive at least two years of compulsory education. All provinces and cities will gradually change the one-year short-term elementary schools in each school district to two-year short-term elementary schools to recruit out-of-school children aged eight to twelve. The principle of adopting a two-part system is still adopted, and the duration of study is one year. By the end of this phase, at least 80% of the total number of school-age children should have received one year of short-term elementary school education or equivalent education.

Phase 3: Starting from August of the 33rd year of the Republic of China, the duration of compulsory education is set at four years, and the two-year short-term elementary schools in various places should be gradually changed to four-year ordinary elementary schools. During the second and third phases, the improvement of private schools and the pilot mobile education should continue to be carried out. (To be continued)

Little Boy (9) 150

— Original by Ms. Alcott of America, translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

"He can play, can't he?" Ned asked, but Tom couldn't speak at that moment because he had just stuffed a steamed apple into his mouth.

Tom had to nod to indicate, but somehow, after a while, he actually started talking again, saying, "Ah, isn't that right? We sometimes dance to his music and do gymnastics. I myself like a bronze drum and want to learn it as soon as possible."

"What I love most is the violin; I can play one too," Ned said, unable to stop confiding in this interesting topic.

"You can?" Tom asked, looking at him with wide eyes full of interest from the edge of his water glass. "Mr. Pei has an old violin, and he'll let you play it if you want."

"You ask if I can? Ah, that's what I miss the most. You see, I used to play the violin with my father and another person all the way to the docks until he died."

"Isn't that interesting?" Tom exclaimed in admiration.

"No, it was terrible; so cold in winter, so hot in summer. I was sometimes tired; they were sometimes annoyed, and I didn't have enough to eat," Ned said, stopping to take a big bite of gingerbread, as if to make himself truly believe that the years of hardship were over; then he said with a regretful expression, "But I did love my violin, and I feel uneasy without it. That person—Old Ni—took it after my father died and didn't want me anymore, saying I was sick."

"If you play well, they will want you to join the band. See what I say here."

"Do you have a band here?" Then Ned's eyes lit up.

"I think so; a lively and happy band, all boys; they sometimes hold concerts and things like that. You just have to watch out for it tomorrow night."

After saying these encouraging words, Tom went back to enjoying his dinner, while Ned gradually delved into flights of fancy, seemingly having no desire to taste the food in front of him.

Sports News

The City Stadium is Fully Completed, A Grand Project with Perfect Layout, Looking Down Upon the Far East, The Library and Museum will also be Completed Next Month 151

In order to seek both sports and prosperity in the city center, the municipal government built a large stadium last year, including a sports field, gymnasium, and swimming pool, in three parts, which have now been fully completed. The Municipal Bureau of Public Works will soon hand it over to the National Games Preparatory Committee for acceptance. In addition, the Library and Museum will also be completed by the end of next month. A reporter from Shen Shi News Agency yesterday explored the situation with the municipal government as follows:

Construction of the Three Parts of the Large Stadium

The large stadium built by the municipal government in the city center started construction in August last year and has now been fully completed. The stadium includes a sports field, gymnasium, and swimming pool, in three parts. The exterior of the sports field is a continuous ring, with a football field in the center, as well as venues for high jump, long jump, ball throwing, and martial arts. It is surrounded by a running track, with the grandstand being about 766 feet long and 17 meters wide, accommodating 40,000 seated and 10,000 standing spectators. Its capacity is about twice that of the Central Stadium. In addition, there are athlete dormitories, offices, exhibition halls, and a wireless broadcasting station. The perfection of the layout can truly look down upon the Far East. The entire project of the stadium has now been completed, with only the running track still under construction.

The Swimming Pool is Equipped with the Most Beautiful Features

The gymnasium can accommodate 3,500 seated and 1,500 standing spectators. If necessary, temporary seats can be added along the walls around the perimeter. The center of the gymnasium is a sports hall, about 23 meters wide and 40 meters long, which can accommodate three ordinary basketball courts. The swimming pool is open-air, accommodating 5,000 spectators. The entire pool is 50 meters long and 20 meters wide, with a capacity of 2,200 cubic meters, holding 600,000 gallons of water. The lighting in the pool consists of strong underwater electric lights, which are not only exceptionally beautiful but also prevent danger. They have now been carefully installed and are fully completed.

The Library and Museum will be Completed Soon

The Municipal Bureau of Public Works, with the entire construction of the large stadium completed and the National Games about to open in February, plans to hand over the stadium to the National Games Preparatory Committee soon. The swimming pool will be filled with water within days and officially opened so that people from all walks of life can go swimming. In addition, the Library and Museum built by the municipal government in the city center also started construction last year. The large projects such as the exterior walls and steel-concrete structures have been completed, and the interior is currently being renovated. Yarn and Cotton: Awaiting the U.S. Cotton Estimate; Little Action from Bulls and Bears in Yarn and Cotton 165

The yarn market, after its recent rapid rises and falls, is gradually showing signs of calm. Today, the market situation is unusually stable, mainly because most investors still expect prices to rise and have not yet released their absorbed positions. As for sellers, seeing that the current yarn market is gradually becoming sluggish and there is no hope of improvement, they are also holding their short positions. Additionally, with the U.S. cotton estimate to be released tomorrow, both bulls and bears are taking a cautious approach. As a result, market transactions are very quiet.

White Luo Creek Cotton Experiences a Sharp Price Increase 167

Yesterday, U.S. cotton opened lower, with prices falling by four to six points across all months. Transactions were mainly for both parties to close out positions in anticipation of the release of the government report. Subsequently, due to selling by foreign firms, cotton farmers selling to lock in profits, and good weather, the market remained weak. After Liverpool made purchases, the government also bought forward cotton to offset the sale of spot cotton from stockpiles. Market prices then recovered. The government report, due to loan issues, would have little impact on market prices unless it was unexpected. Finally, long positions for October contracts were closed out, and the market price fell sharply by twelve points. Prices for the remaining months fell by one to two points. Spot prices fell by ten points. British spot cotton fell by one point, and futures fell by one to two points. Indian seven and eight-month white Luo Creek cotton saw prices rise sharply due to shortages. Pingguo cotton rose sharply by 1.75 rupees, Aomula rose by 0.25 rupees, white Luo Creek rose by 4.75 rupees, and far-term contracts rose by 0.25 rupees. Free Talk

The World Through a Pin Hole 176

— Yu

The world seen through a pinhole might actually exist as such: viewing Mount Tai as a small hill, and Sumeru as a mustard seed. The objective world is certainly not that small; however, the world of man is certainly not that large. In the man-made world, the world you can perceive to exist is only the size of a pinhole. Thus, all you can know is: how much is a liter of rice, how much is a pound of firewood, how much is a foot of cloth, where there's easy money to be made, and where there are women to be had. If you fall short of this standard, you're a fool. If you exceed this standard, you're a heretic. A fool is at most material for jokes, but for a heretic, the "ancient" method is "to punish according to the law." The Pharisees crucifying Jesus is a perfect example of this. Fools provide material for jokes, and heretics uphold the dignity of the law. A few fools, a few heretics, dealt with using ancient methods, sent to the cross, or "banished to distant lands," and the integrity of society is no longer a problem. However, people are not uniform. Each has their own face. Even if you use the Spartan method of killing infants to force uniformity, human power is ultimately finite. There are countless fools, and not a few heretics either. This is difficult. On the other hand, even if you consider yourself qualified, some European eugenicists, supposedly based on biology, assert their scholarly authority and bluntly declare people of color to be inferior races. Whether this theory is correct or not, our pedantic scholars, self-proclaimed authorities of the ×× school, often pick up the leftovers of foreigners, saying our race is this way or that way. If that's the case, wouldn't we all become fools, or threats to white culture? When that time comes, the problem will be quite serious.

Naturally, the few white people who say this have their own purposes, and whether we believe this doctrine is up to us. If you believe it and are willing to be ranked as inferior, that's another matter. If you don't believe it and want to strive for a better future, you must kick this slanderous rhetoric away. But there's a prerequisite: when this race faces unprecedented danger, our eyes should leave the pinhole, and the world we observe should not be about how much is a liter of rice, how much is a pound of firewood, how much is a foot of cloth, where to find easy money, or where to find women. Individual existence is finite, but the continuation of the race is infinite. The question is whether to seek personal enjoyment in the present, or to pursue the infinite continuation of the community. If we take the former path, then there's no need to recognize anything. If we take the latter path, we must use the strength of a lion fighting a bull to fight against external forces and natural disasters. The crux lies in this process. Therefore, the current period is just as Dickens said at the beginning of "A Tale of Two Cities": "It was the best of times, it was the worst of times,... it was the season of Light, it was the season of Darkness, it was the spring of hope, it was the winter of despair, we had everything before us, we had nothing before us, we were all going direct to Heaven, we were all going direct the other way..." These words can explain everything about this era. However, we certainly don't need to despair or fear. Social change is the process of social evolution. H.G. Wells said in the preface to his book "The Work, Wealth and Happiness of Mankind": "...all of us are only now beginning to realize that we are living in the decadence of any system of our age, in a chaos, from which a new one will grow. All kinds of forces are currently carrying out the work of disintegration, but at the same time, they are constructing a new atmosphere of a larger, stranger institution, where we will adapt to life." Dispelling the old and bringing forth the new is an inevitable process. And the only task for people, as the driving force of society, is to broaden their horizons, exert their human power, gather together, and fulfill their human responsibilities!

Welcoming Mei 177

— Cao Juren

Dr. Mei Lanfang is said to have returned with honors.

Among the clamorous voices, there are several viewpoints: A says that since Chinese opera is so popular in Europe, it must have a bright future. B says that Dr. Mei's return from Europe will lead him to adopt the strengths of European drama to compensate for the weaknesses of Chinese opera, creating a new form of opera with Chinese opera as the foundation and Western drama as the application. C says that Dr. Mei is to Europeans what African savages are, merely a curiosity, and its significance is no greater than Landauer's around-the-world tour. It would be an exaggeration to overestimate or underestimate Mei Lanfang's European tour. It would be a delusion to think that Mei Lanfang's drama will cause a major change in the European opera scene, and it would be too much to expect that Dr. Mei's hasty tour would bring about major changes in Chinese opera. Of course, it is also a half-baked opinion to say that Dr. Mei's tour was completely meaningless, and we cannot agree with that.

The form of art is often renewed: adding a transformation to an extremely old form creates a brand new style. It's like a cheongsam worn by a modern girl, it doesn't feel out of place. The currents of world art, East and West, have always irrigated each other and cannot be separated. For example, Guanyin Bodhisattva contains elements of Greek mythology, adds Indian colors, and is then painted in China. No one can say it belongs to a specific time or place. Western opera has inherited many artistic forms from the Hebrews and Egyptians, and Chinese opera has absorbed artistic forms from the Western Regions and India. Russia, located between Europe and Asia, has long been infused with Eastern colors. Mei Lanfang's performance may make them pay more attention to the form of Chinese opera, which is not impossible. On the other hand, Mei Lanfang saw many Western opera forms, and it is natural for him to use them to change the form of Chinese opera. But these are all gradual improvements, and the opera world will not be stirred up by this, and Chinese opera will not have a bright future because of this.

What I want to ask Dr. Mei is: has Dr. Mei made any changes to the content of the opera, which belongs to the conscious part? Speaking of opera, Qilin Tong's "Nine Watch" can indeed move the audience; the advertisement often sees the words "Nine Watch replaces rolling on nail boards." But that is a script that promotes feudal philosophy. Although there is still the fact that landlords take turns to serve in rotation, and the slave system still exists everywhere, we will never admit that "substituting for rolling on a nail board" has the meaning of "human." Another example is the auspicious opera "Hundred Longevity Pictures," which should clearly depict the tyranny of warlords and the grief of the emperor in a declining era, but it is performed as the princess's dignity is inviolable, and the emperor acts as a mediator, and then the couple reconciles as before, its distortion of facts has long lost the meaning of the times. The decline of Chinese opera is not the decline of form, but the decline of content. Old opera takes the protection of the morality of the rural patriarchal society as its only mission. Since the rural patriarchal society has completely collapsed, the flowers growing on that land have naturally withered. If Dr. Mei's view of social reality has not been thoroughly changed, and the content of the opera has not been completely changed, any kind of improvement is in vain.

I don't have too high expectations for Dr. Mei, I only hope that he will not let down this trip to Russia.

Guan Zi Jiao Seaside 178

— Fei Er

Penang, I haven't seen you for half a year. I went to Guan Zi Jiao Seaside. It was night, and the lighthouse flashed a ray of sunlight on the sea. The tide of the Penang Strait played a low and tranquil tune. The breeze gently blew on the back of the chair where I was sitting, and the coast of the Malay Peninsula in the distance shimmered with faint lights. The world was in darkness, the sounds of the city in Penang's residential area were unusually low, and the sea gently kissed the coast with a hypnotic melody. Stars twinkled in the sky, and the beautiful sea surface played the music played by the music pavilion behind. An exchange of natural and human sounds, blended into a harmonious rhythm. The soft air, the melodious music, the gentle tide, and the bright light emitted by the lighthouse, all converged into the beauty of Guan Zi Jiao Seaside. If the sea of Singapore is magnificent and heroic, then the thin slice of sea in Guan Zi Jiao is delicate and gentle. The tide of Singapore stirs up people's ambition and enthusiasm, while the sea of Penang teaches people to sink into the deep realm of art. The bright sea surface of Singapore allows people to unfold the wings of deep fantasy, while the beautiful sea surface of Penang teaches people to open the eyes of artists. If the sea of Singapore is lovely, then the sea of Penang is no less nostalgic.

The next day, I also went to the seaside called Fun. That is completely a rustic seaside scene. In front of the sea lies a vast beach, and the afternoon sun turns the fine sand into gold. The shore is pillowed by a large expanse of green, and scattered figures float in the sea water. In the distance, faint city sounds occasionally drifted in, and the chirping of birds resounded clearly. Occasionally, a sail floated on the sea, and a wisp of light white clouds floated in the sky. The air here is as silent as in the evening, and the sea lies quietly, as if in a deep sleep.

The entire coastline of Penang is under the overlook of the beautiful mountains, and the Penang Strait is sandwiched into a dark green brocade ribbon. Although it has lost the magnificent appearance of the sea, I love it like a noble work of art.

Child 179

— Chai Dake

The child is six years old, growing up day by day, very lively; he is also naughty, and like other children, he wants to eat and play. Not satisfied with eating his fill, he urges his mother for more. He plays when he grows up, and doesn't know fatigue. When he plays hard, he even forgets to eat. His mother's calls remind him, and then he goes to the table listlessly. He is happy when he laughs, and he cries when he is angry, just like other children. He doesn't know resentment. All he does is look at the older brothers, younger brothers, older sisters, and younger sisters next door, and he feels envy because he doesn't have any. But he doesn't have any after all, so he is angry and hateful, and when he hates fiercely, he vents his anger by crying. According to his mother, she told him: "Other people's older brothers, younger brothers, older sisters, and younger sisters cannot be taken away and considered Baby's; just like Baby's ball, wooden gun, and bayonet are Baby's, and cannot be taken away by others. Baby is born from Mama: is Mama's, so Mama loves!" The child doesn't know what older brothers, younger brothers, older sisters, and younger sisters are all about. All he knows is that only Mama belongs to him; he belongs to Mama, but he feels that the older brothers, younger brothers, older sisters, and younger sisters next door are very cute; he gets along well with them, so he loves to play with them. Of course! They also love this adorable child. The child is afraid to approach, only the mother of the children next door.

"Beggar... little rascal..." The mother of the children next door often scolds the child like this. "Beggars are such disgusting things." The child thinks, "Isn't that the kind of dirty, skinny one?"

"It would be great if I had an older brother or sister!" Whenever he feels lonely, he always hopes for this. If the hope is realized, who says? Isn't this child the happy one? But he is permanently immersed in this resentment. Only when he plays with the older brothers and sisters next door... does he temporarily forget this resentment, but when he is thinking about something alone, this resentment immediately enters his little chest.

"The older brothers and sisters next door... are together all day long. If Baby had an older brother or sister, he could also play in the same room all day long; eat at the same table: sleep on the same bed!" When his mother goes shopping, he is truly lonely! He needs one or two older brothers, older sisters, younger brothers, and younger sisters!" The child is somewhat suspicious and asks his mother, "Since the children next door are not Baby's older brothers, older sisters, younger brothers, and younger sisters, why does Baby call them older brothers, older sisters, younger brothers, and younger sisters?" Although the child feels that the children next door treat him very well; and at the same time, they are calling each other affectionately.

"Call if you want, but they are not Baby's older brothers, older sisters, younger brothers, and younger sisters after all! Baby's older brother... is...?" His mother answers with tears in her eyes. The child is very strange! Whenever he mentions wanting an older brother or sister, his mother always chokes up and can't speak! The child feels that his mother's sobs are cute, that she can sympathize with him for not having an older brother or sister! Unlike the mother of the children next door, who hits and scolds people at the drop of a hat! And separates his only playmates.

The child doesn't like to see his mother's often sullen face, and he never hears his mother's giggling laughter. He is happy; his mother is not necessarily happy. Only when he is naughty; his mother will put on a funny face and smile to tease the child to laugh. When the child is learning to read, his mother is also smiling. The child realizes that only learning to read can bring out his mother's smile, because the child likes to see his mother's smile.

The children next door wear flowered and red clothes; their hats are inlaid with sparkling glass pieces, which look very good. The child also loves them, only hating that he always wears white trousers; a black hat; and a blue short shirt, such plain colors. Isn't that right! That day, the child clamored for a red jacket, and his mother cut a short jacket out of a piece of red old cloth for the child on the street.

"The older brothers and younger brothers next door... are coming to snatch Baby's red cloth jacket! Mama! I... I won't give it to them!" That night, he woke up from his dream screaming like this, because this red cloth jacket was his only beloved thing. The father of the children next door always has to come home a few times after a long time, and he always brings back some toys and food to make the children happy. Isn't that a tall figure, just like the chauffeur of the family across the street!" The child remembers it this way, but the shadow of the child's father has never returned. The child has never seen a tall man. He is his ideal father. According to his mother, "Daddy is making money in a very far place." The child thinks: Daddy not only doesn't love him; but he also doesn't love Mama, otherwise, why doesn't he come back to see Mama! Because he sees his mother cry when she talks about Daddy.

The child thinks: "Daddy is really a scary animal. Aren't the children next door often beaten by their daddy and scream loudly! Aren't their butts all black and blue!"

"Daddy must be a terrible person!" The dad of the children next door is making money; the child's dad is also making money; making money is the same; so the fierceness is also the same. He firmly affirms that Daddy is such an animal. Thinking of Daddy makes him afraid, he tries his best to push the fantasy out of his mind, but the more he thinks about it, the more afraid he becomes, and he has nightmares at night, dreaming of a strange and ferocious man hitting him hard. Fortunately, Daddy never comes back, which makes him half relieved.

The child also connects that his mother cries whenever she talks about Daddy, definitely because Daddy hit Mama. In this way, the child firmly hopes that his daddy will never come back, but at the same time, he needs an older brother who is as lovable as Mama...

University Days (4) (1) 180

— Written by the German Storm translated by Chen Yinzhi

We walked through the shady path into the forest, and were almost to the path leading to the dance house, when we saw a crowd of people gathered on the beach from the other side of the woods. They were standing close to the water, seemingly busy placing something unclear on the ground. At this moment, a man in fishing clothes came up the mountain. "What's going on down there!" I asked casually.

"Not a good thing, sir!" he replied, "A young girl drowned."

"Nelly ah!" I shouted, unconsciously grabbing Fritz's hand.

He shouted in fright. "What are you saying!" he said, to cover up his feelings.

At the same time, we intimately walked through the woods down to the beach. On the road, I heard the crowd below talking about this. "What was wrong with her?" a rough male voice said. "This is probably a noble lady, you see she jumped into the water dressed neatly." Then there was no sound, only the sound of waves rolling in the morning air.

When we came out of the woods, the entire bay was covered in sunlight, and I was almost dizzy from being illuminated by it. She also lay under this sunlight. As we approached, the fishermen made way to the side; we could see her clearly. Without any obstruction. Was it really her? There was no longer any doubt! A pale face rested on the beach; a pair of dancing feet now motionless protruded from under her clothes; a head of wet black hair was covered with seaweed and shells. The white rose was no longer there, perhaps it had fallen to the bottom of the sea.

Many years have passed since that early morning. — In the churchyard of the university town, next to the tall grass, lies a white marble stele, with the words "Lelyna Bolika" engraved on it. — This stele was erected by three fellow villagers scattered throughout Germany. (End)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

The Heroic Deeds of Huaian Xin'an Elementary School Students 181

— Xing An

We still remember that two years ago, seven elementary school students from Huaian Qin'an Elementary School automatically organized a tour group to travel to Shanghai. The purpose of their organizing this tour group was to experience real social life and break the adult notion of distrusting children. They came out to travel without adult leadership, and all their daily life, food, and drink were managed by themselves. As soon as they arrived in Shanghai, they immediately became active, socializing, visiting, and giving speeches, just like an adult tour group, and everything was handled in an orderly manner. At that time, it attracted the attention of the general public.

Two years have passed, and now more noteworthy news has come. This time, Xin'an Elementary School has even greater ambitions, and their journey is much longer, a ten-province tour. The tour group this time has more than ten members. The oldest is nineteen years old, and the youngest is twelve years old. The time is tentatively set for three months. The travel destinations are ten provinces, including Lu, Ji, Cha, Sui, Shan, Yu, Wan, E, and Xiang. All expenses are borne by these elementary school students themselves, maintained by the income from selling books and giving speeches along the way. When necessary, they will show movies and play phonographs to carry out various publicity activities. It is said that all matters are now ready, and they can start off around the beginning of next month. This is truly an amazing feat.

Originally, school life cannot be completely separated from social life. Society is the school. In addition to receiving school education, a student must also personally experience various practical aspects of social life from time to time, in order to prepare for joining society and becoming active after leaving school. However, in our country's education, society is society. Schools and society are too far apart, almost as unrelated as the wind and the horse. This point should be improved. Xin'an Elementary School's two-time organization of tour groups, giving students the opportunity to experience social life in the field, this meaning is very significant.

However, although the intention of elementary school students to hold long-distance travel is good, this behavior is inevitably too risky. A ten-province tour is something even adults are afraid to try, and it is even more difficult for children. Moreover, in our country, transportation is inconvenient, the local area is not peaceful, and there are many obstacles along the way. Without sufficient guidance and safe measures, it is impossible to put people at ease. The school authorities should consider this point.

Finally, we hope that this ten-province tour of Xin'an Elementary School students will be a great success, leaving a glorious record in this children's year.

Cuiheng Village 182

— Ai Tu

Cuiheng Village—the hometown of Mr. Sun Yat-sen, what an enchanting name! It holds the breath of greatness, with exquisite flavors. I carried a heart of longing and traveled from the distant city to that place.

Leaving the bustling Shiqi, I boarded a long-distance bus of the Qiguan Company at the bus station on the pier. After purchasing a ticket to Cuiheng Village, I let the bus speed southward on the flat highway as if it were crazy. At that time, looking out the window, all I could see were expanses of plains and vast fields, with villages standing on the edges of the plains or hills. Sparse green forests seemed to express a melancholic sigh as the southern sea breeze rustled, like a sigh of joy—at this moment, although my eyes were watching the quickly passing suburban scenery, my mind was filled with the great historical relics of Cuiheng Village, filled with the thought of the many children who always greeted people with cheerful laughter there... everything possessed me.

Along the way, the carriage sped along, passing through high mountains and ornate villages that mixed the old and new. There, I could see many poetic pictures. Sometimes, by the babbling streams, I could see innocent and lively girls carrying baskets to the stones by the stream to wash clothes. Their completely sorrowless smiling faces revealed a captivating aura, and their innocent and adorable eyes blinked as they stared at the bus passing by them. Sometimes, their graceful, shy bodies danced joyfully, sending out interesting laughter. All of this truly made people who had grown up in the city feel that living in the countryside was very happy. Also, they wore large hats with a style different from other places, hats that only men wore in other villages. The tall, pointed, and wide bamboo hats, sometimes with a bit of decorative flair, worn slightly askew, showed a healthy demeanor that was absolutely different from the delicate and artificial posture of the daughters of big cities, who had lost their innocence.

The car traveled at high speed for about two hours before arriving at Cuiheng Village. I got out of the car and rested in a pavilion, inhaling the wind blowing from the mountains and the sea. At that time, my gaze fell on the small village below the forest, which was Cuiheng Village—not a very large village. The back mountain was covered with vast and lush green forests, and the whistling sound coming from the treetops was so energetic and rustling. The village's style was no different from other villages, perhaps in the style of the eighteenth century, but it was not dilapidated, and very stable. On the left side of the village, near the open space, were two slightly taller houses, which were the home of the President. It is said that he was from a prominent family in his childhood, and indeed, this historical trace is still very clearly left before our eyes. Therefore, their home was always a little more beautiful and exquisite than other homes.

In front of Cuiheng Village is a vast field, where the President must have been accustomed to playing in his childhood. Not far from the village across, there is a very quiet stream, and the banks of the stream are lined with green trees that are not very big. It is very possible to drive a small boat on the surface of the water. This is where the President threw the tablet of the local god into the water in his youth. The stream winds around, and far away, it makes people feel the beauty of the quiet countryside. Even in summer, this is still a place that can be used as a summer resort.

Next to Cuiheng Village is the new school building of "Mr. Sun Yat-sen Memorial School," tall, with red bricks and green tiles, with the Western flavor of the new century. When I went there, several teachers happily took me to see various places, and I also felt that their teaching performance would not be bad. Therefore, my heart was even more joyful.

While I was in the village, when the innocent and lively children followed us, smiling and asking questions, they were so friendly, unlike strangers, and took me to wander around many mountains, forests, and riverbanks. They also told interesting stories of the President's childhood with laughter, such as where the President loved the most. At this time, I was completely like a child who did not know sadness, laughing and jumping along with them. —Those lovely children have a demeanor different from other places!

In the afternoon, when the sun was about to set behind the forest, I left the lovely Cuiheng Village and boarded the bus again, hurrying towards the south.

Summer Evening 183

— Hua Zhi

Summer evenings are the most comfortable time of day. Being cooped up in the office all day like a roasted duck, the numbers and documents almost made my head spin. Even though the fan never stopped spinning overhead, I couldn't feel any coolness from the wind, as if a warm current was about to engulf me. Moreover, something was twitching in my temples, and I felt nauseous, not even having time to chew on a Baifeng pill. In this way, I had to endure for eight whole hours, just like a prisoner who had lost his freedom, unable to control myself at all. Although I could lie on the sofa and steal a little laziness during the two hours after dinner, the sweat stains on my back were always slippery and uncomfortable. Naturally, what everyone hopes for is the evening.

For example: when you return home like a fugitive, the most urgent task is naturally to take a bath. So you suddenly—like a quick-handed magician, strip off all your clothes and jump into the bathtub. The bathtub is filled with just the right amount of warm water, and as you soak your tired body, you might forget that it is already evening outside with a myriad of lights. You enjoy this

Page 18

indescribable comfort, like a dream, until your family calls you to have dinner, and then you feel that time has passed too quickly.

Then, after drying your whole body, your spirit is completely restored, and you put on thin clothes and have dinner in the courtyard. Your family must have prepared your favorite dishes especially for you, and if you are married, you have a child who can just hop and skip around. The pleasure of a family cannot be greater than this.

At this time, a moon like a new bud is hanging in the eastern corner of the sky, and the heat on the ground has also dissipated. You can open the door wide and let the cool evening breeze blow around your dining table. After a happy dinner, you move the dining table away, and everyone lies back in rattan chairs. And there must be herbal tea prepared for you to quench your thirst after dinner, or even half a leftover watermelon. And your child? He will not allow you to lie down quietly, but at this time, your spirit is very comfortable. You are very happy to tell him stories. You can make up whatever you want about Brother Cow and Sister Cat, but the child is very willing to listen. If you are in a better situation, and you can rent a larger yard, of course you will be very happy to plant some flowers and trees: the morning glories climbing on the high walls are the easiest flowers to grow. Just scatter some seeds along the base of the wall, attach them to the high wall with a few grass ropes, and they will quickly fill the entire wall with flowers. It is most pleasing to the eye to see more flowers and trees in summer. When you return from the office, you can also take a walk in the yard, watching them being scorched by the day's scorching sun, turning into a haggard woman, and you will feel a little sorry in your heart. But when the moon rises, they, like your spirit, have regained their former appearance: the drooping ones have raised their heads, and the withered ones have also released their flowers. Although they are all flowers and plants without fragrance, they have a fresh fragrance in the evening breeze. Around the yard, balsams and cockscombs are also indispensable, red flowers, green leaves; if you can plant a few pots of lotus flowers, that would be even better, with white flowers blooming on straight stems, and their fragrance is truly refreshing. In this situation, even if there is a lot of important work waiting for you to do, you will never be willing to leave. Smoking a cigarette, closing your eyes slightly, the stuffiness you suffered in the office just now has long since disappeared without a trace. After your child has heard enough stories, he is snuggling in his mother's arms, and perhaps in a few minutes, he is already snoring softly, fast asleep. Because it is after dinner, your wife will not let him sleep, so she calls him, shouts him, listens to Daddy tell stories, or eats watermelon, using all kinds of methods to wake him up, but children are the most free people in the world, and if he wants to sleep, there is no way to wake him up. Then, take him to the bedroom, but in the time it takes for your wife to go back and forth, you yourself will involuntarily fall asleep. When you are awakened, you will definitely not be able to help but laugh, and then stagger into the house. A lovely summer evening has passed quietly like this.

Boat Girl 184

— Da

The sun rests on the distant peaks of the dark green mountains in the west, like a burning red gong, listlessly drilling into the back of the mountains. Suddenly, the western sky burned with bloody clouds over most of the sky, with clusters of dark and beautifully scaled clouds.

Waves of crows, like a disbanded group of soldiers, flew from this side of the river to the jungle on the opposite bank without discipline, cawing and chirping, flying and desperately blowing their mouths, chattering enough to be annoying! However, it seemed to carry another kind of mission—awakening another group of pitiful people.

"Ruixiang, get up, it's not early... Hurry up and get dressed, look, the sun has already sunk behind the mountains." A plump, forty-year-old woman dressed in a short silk shirt and trousers was bending over at the stern of the boat, wiping the floor very carefully, cleaning the vases and teacups. She looked up at the sky and shouted loudly. At the same time, she seemed extremely tired, panting like an old ox working in the fields, muttering to herself, "It's really getting worse every year, I never thought that the things the old woman did would now be taken on by myself!"

Ruixiang woke up from her sleep, stretched lazily, calmed her mind, and then pushed open the small window on the left side of the boat, sticking out half of her melon-seed-shaped head to look around: the sky was clear, floating with light and fluffy clouds; the water was as green as distant mountains, rippling with fine waves. She thought in her heart, "The weather is so good, and it just happens to be the fifteenth night, the Moon Sister is growing a full, round face, so charming. With such a good time and beautiful scenery, it seems that tonight's business is definitely going to earn her dozens of silver dollars..." Thinking this, her heart blossomed, she smiled, pursed her mouth for a moment, and gave a charming cat-like wink, and quickly went to the dressing table to tidy up her disheveled hair that resembled a clump of grass.

The night breath gradually sank down, and the dim shadows of dusk, like an ambush of soldiers, slowly crawled out from where they were encountered, swallowing the distant dark green evening mountains. At this time, Ruixiang rested her right hand on her cheek, sitting in the front of the flower boat, looking very delicate and charming! Her face brushed against the colorful clouds in the sky, and her eyebrows were like two curved black lines. She was wearing a soft, thin silk cheongsam, her chest was very full, and the tips of her two new grave-like breasts stood out stiffly, as if they were about to pierce through this soft, thin silk clothing. She caught sight of the passing tourists on the shore, and threw a not-very-natural, seductive smile at them, like a foxy siren, trying to arouse their affections. However, despite her best efforts to throw seductive smiles, no one was willing to easily board the flower boat.

The moon slowly rose from the treetops on the opposite bank, full and round like a white jade plate, bright and clean, and suddenly a winding, endless silver snake rippled across the heart of the river. Although it was the dog days of June, it was still a cool place at night, and there was no need for palm-leaf fans. The cool breeze gently blew, bringing with it the fragrant aroma of the longan flowers on the opposite bank. This aroma had once intoxicated Ruixiang's heart, making her feel the preciousness and joy of life. However, now, the aroma of the longan flowers was still so fragrant and rich, but her state of mind was not the same as it was three years ago. She began to feel disappointed and tired, her head drooped heavily, and she sank very sadly into the dream of three years ago. The girls on the flower boats lived a life of singing and drinking, but who could have predicted that her door would be so desolate three years later, after the luxury of that life, the liveliness of the business, and the prominence of her reputation? To say that she was old and no longer attracting people's attention, Ruixiang would never dare to believe this reason. She often looked at herself in the mirror, and everything was no different from three years ago, her flesh was still fat and plump. What was the reason for the sluggish business? To say that it was because of the collection of flower donations, song donations, and feast donations... which made the people who frequented the boats reluctant to come, and they had no interest, this was not a sufficient reason! However, the sluggish business was already a fact, but what exactly was the reason, in Ruixiang's heart, it was an unanswerable mystery.

The night was deep, the moon hung coquettishly in the middle of the sky, and the tourists on the shore were sparse. Ruixiang quietly went into the flower boat with a heart full of disappointment.

Kidnapped (Part 1) 185

— Lin Hao

The fields in the twilight presented a golden glow, the remaining radiance of the setting sun shining from the west of Da Niuyao Ridge. The evening breeze gently brought the warmth of midsummer, and fine grains of dust. Having taken a mule cart from Shalan all day, my buttocks felt a bit sore from the cobblestone path; moreover, I noticed the struggling of that poor mule, its hooves hitting like they were striking tens of millions of pounds of steel, and its large nostrils exhaling such rapid breaths; so I said to the mule driver who was whipping it: "Hey, friend, it's not early anyway! It's too late to rush, why not find an inn and stay overnight? Look, the mule is tired enough!"

"Yes, that's what I was thinking too, but let's hurry up a bit more, if we just drive the mule cart into Liuying Village, there will be inns there." The pockmarked mule driver raised his whip, a faint smile appearing at the corner of his mouth.

It was already evening when we drove into Liuying Village. We stayed at a larger inn. The owner was such a kind old man, although he was already old, his health and spirit were worthy of admiration; especially his cheerful conversational skills, with none of the current merchant's reserve.

Late at night. I pushed open the window, which was facing the inn's courtyard. In front of the window grew a low little tree. Looking through the gaps in the branches, I could see a round moon in the dark sky, and a few flickering stars; quietly, I couldn't hear any sound. Occasionally, I heard one or two howls of dogs, and the low moans of night owls. In my heart, there rose a lonely, melancholic thought: serene, mournful!

Suddenly, a series of "bang, bang, crash" sounds in the distance startled me from the lonely silence. I stared at the distant mountain range lying in the black atmosphere—where the sounds seemed to originate—my whole body trembled as if possessed by a demon. Unconsciously, I entered a realm of terror; at the time when I was recalling my past experiences, I subconsciously determined that it was the sound of gunfire.

"Get up, guests, get up quickly!" When I discovered the old owner's soft cry, my terror increased, because this was certainly the same as what I had just thought, and I also realized that the old owner's voice was so slightly trembling with panic. I gradually stood up my numb body, and walked out of the room step by step. Many guests had already gathered outside the door; everyone was holding a strange heart: "Hey, you, old owner, what's all the fuss about in the middle of the night?"

Liu Xiang's Preface to the Strategies of the Warring States (5)

Therefore, the Confucian scholars like Mencius and Xun Qing were abandoned by the world, while the strategists who traveled and persuaded were valued by the common people. Thus, Su Qin, Zhang Yi, Gongsun Yan, Chen Zhen, Dai, Li, and their like advocated the doctrines of alliances and disjunctions, using short and long strategies to influence states. Su Qin advocated alliances, while Zhang Yi advocated disjunction. If disjunction prevailed, Qin would become emperor; if alliances prevailed, Chu would become king. The state where they resided would be valued, while the state they left would be disregarded. However, at that time, the Qin state was the most powerful, while the other states were weak. Su Qin united them, forming a coalition of six states to resist Qin, causing everyone to fear and not dare to peep at its soldiers in the region within the passes. The world was free from war for twenty-nine years.

News 191

The Yinshe Drama Troupe is organized by Zhao Guangyao, Wei Hongen, Yang Yifei, and others. The troupe has been preparing for a long time and is large in scale. It has now selected several historical and folk drama scripts that are beneficial to education. It is reported that they will be broadcast on major radio stations in Shanghai soon. The troupe is also recruiting four female members. Anyone with aspirations and a love of art can participate. Applications must include a half-body photo and a brief resume, and should be sent to Yang Yifei, c/o Shipping Radio Station, 93 Guangdong Road, Shanghai. Applications that do not meet the requirements will be returned.

Since social comedians Jiang Xiaoxiao and Bao Lele started broadcasting on the radio, they have been welcomed by all listeners. Recently, Jiang and Bao have compiled all their comedic jokes and lyrics from the past decade into a special publication called "Jiang Bao's Collection of Jokes." The content is extremely rich and will be published soon. Sample copies of "Jiang Bao's Collection of Jokes" are being distributed to various sectors. Listeners who wish to obtain a sample copy should write to the two comedians c/o the Great China Radio Station on Nanjing Road. The postage is five cents for addresses within Shanghai and six cents for addresses outside of Shanghai.

The sound film "The Peach Blossom Fan" makes a great sacrifice. Lianhua will fight against the current of economic depression with the great efforts of all its colleagues, hoping to jointly save the fate of domestic films, and sincerely hope that the film industry, the audience, and the film media will work together.

During the filming of "Wild Geese Descending on the Cold River" at the Japan studio, the interior of the newlyweds' new home was filmed, and joy filled the photography studio.

The cast of "Tian Lun" almost includes all the stars of Lianhua.

Yang Xiaozhong's directed "Four Sisters" is about to be completed. Previously, the Carlton Theater was borrowed to film the stage scene, with nearly 200 actors working all night.

A beautiful small fan will be given to every audience member during the premiere of "Little Angel."

Liu Jijun and Fei Boqing both play important roles in "Four Sisters."

Mingyueshe's Lin Linlang will perform "Wild Rose" at the Central Theater today.

Publishing World 194

The second issue of Junyi Pictorial, published by Baiyun Printing House at 29 Aierjin Road, Luderun Lane, is published today. The content is more exquisite than the previous issue. The photography includes Mei Lanfang's hobbies and recent situation among European stars, and the military actions of Italy and A country. The text includes the story of the Five Tiger Chenzhi, Ye Juanjuan's unfortunate humor and satire, etc. There are also more than ten caricatures by Hua Yifei and others, with Cao Hanmei's "Wine, Sex, Wealth, and Temper" being the most valuable. The Children's Literature Magazine, located at 44-46 Fengyuan Lane, Tangshan Road, Shanghai, is organized by famous children's book writers Lin Yin, He Gongchao, Du Yemu, etc. In view of the opening of Children's Year and the urgent need for children's books, they have specially compiled and printed a Children's Literature Magazine. The first issue is scheduled to be published on the 20th of this month. The content is exceptionally exciting, and the price is extremely low. It is published every half month, with 24 issues per year, costing only one yuan including postage. Pre-orders before September 1st do not require a deposit and can receive an 20% discount, and will also receive two volumes of picture story detectives. Subscriptions can be made at the Shanghai Miscellaneous Knot Company's Shenbao Service Department and the magazine's publishing department.

"Little Angel" Premieres Today 195

Lianhua director Wu Yonggang became famous with the film "The Goddess." Now he is launching his new work "Little Angel," proving that with the excellent achievements in "The Goddess," it can be expected that he will make extraordinary contributions. "Little Angel" was commissioned by the Jiangsu Provincial Government. Chen Guofu, the chairman of the provincial government, has vigorously promoted the educational film industry in recent years. He once handed over his own script to various film companies to be made into films. Recently, he openly solicited scripts and selected "Little Angel" from hundreds of submissions as the first choice. Chen believed that Lianhua had the most outstanding achievements in film production, so he handed it over to the company for filming. The company then assigned the most outstanding directors and actors to produce it, taking five months to complete. With Lianhua's reputation, coupled with the cooperation of director Wu Yonggang and actors Wang Renmei, Lin Chuchu, etc., the excellent results can be imagined. The film is now scheduled to premiere at the Jincheng Grand Theater today.
